# Core RNG Roadmap

This document tracks `alea` against the long-term product goal in `AGENTS.md`:
surpass Rust `rand` / `rand_distr` in core random-number functionality using
Zig-native designs.

It is a living roadmap, not a completion certificate. When all milestones in one
stage are closed, define the next stricter stage instead of declaring the
broader product goal permanently finished.
`compare/results/active-goal-completion-audit.md` records the current
thread-level non-completion audit.

The active product focus is the current Linux environment. The goal for each
stage is to drive this platform to no known core RNG gaps against locally
available Rust `rand` / `rand_distr` evidence before expanding to broader
platform and longer-run requirements.

## Covered

| Area | Alea artifact | Evidence |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Deterministic engines | `Alea4x64`, `Wyhash64`, `Xoshiro128PlusPlus`, `Xoshiro256`, `Xoshiro256PlusPlus`, `Pcg64`, `SplitMix64`, `StepRng`, `ChaCha8Rng`, `ChaCha20Rng`, and Rust-discoverable `SmallRng` alias | Engine unit tests and `zig build test` |
| ChaCha streams | `ChaCha8Rng`, `ChaCha12` engine, Rust-discoverable `ChaCha12Rng` / `StdRng` aliases, `ChaCha20Rng`, and `secure(io)` | `src/engines/chacha.zig`, `src/engines/chacha8.zig`, `src/engines/chacha20.zig`, `src/root.zig` |
| System entropy | `Seed.secure`, `defaultSecure`, `fastSecure`, `scalarSecure`, `hashSecure`, `reproducibleSecure`, `secureBytes`, `SysRng`, `SysError`, `sysRng`, and explicit-I/O root random/fill helpers | `src/seed.zig`, `src/root.zig`, `src/rng.zig` |
| `std.Random` interop | Engine `random()` methods and `Rng.random()` | `src/root.zig`, `src/rng.zig` |
| Scalar sampling | integers, floats, booleans, ranges, durations, allocation-returning scalar/vector range, scalar/vector strict-interval, scalar/vector probability, and duration batches, ratio/chance, chance/ratio fill and vector sampling, caller-owned and allocation-returning bytes | `src/rng.zig` tests |
| Structured sampling | arrays, tuples, enums | `Rng.value(T)` tests |
| Repeated sampling | `valueBatch`, `valueBatchChecked`, `sampleBatch`, `normalBatch`, `exponentialBatch`, `valueIter`, `randomIter`, `sampleIter` | `src/rng.zig` tests |
| Unicode and strings | ASCII charsets, custom `Charset`, reusable Unicode scalar `UnicodeCharset`, Unicode scalar UTF-8 strings with allocation-returning and caller-owned-buffer helpers | `src/ascii.zig` tests |
| Uniform samplers | `Uniform(T)`, `Open01`, `OpenClosed01`, distribution-namespace vector uniform and strict-interval wrappers plus reusable vector samplers | `src/distributions.zig` tests |
| Bernoulli/binomial/hypergeometric | `Bernoulli`, `VectorBernoulli`, `Binomial`, `VectorBinomial`, `NegativeBinomial`, `VectorNegativeBinomial`, `Hypergeometric`, `VectorHypergeometric`, direct-source reusable sampling, distribution-layer scalar/vector bulk fills | Moment and parameter tests |
| Continuous distributions | normal, exact log-normal, bounded f32 approximate log-normal, half-normal, exponential, gamma, chi-squared, chi, erlang, beta, Fisher F, Student t, triangular, arcsine, cauchy, laplace, logistic, log-logistic, kumaraswamy, power-function, rayleigh, maxwell, pareto, weibull, dirichlet, standard/derived distribution fill APIs, unit geometry fill APIs | Sampler tests and moment smoke tests |
| Poisson/geometric | small-lambda exact product method, large-lambda PTRS method, geometric/failures/standard-geometric, cached reusable samplers, scalar/vector bulk fills | Large-lambda moment and support tests |
| Sequence sampling | compact `IndexVec` with lazy/caller-owned/allocation-returning value/pointer item mapping, checked mutable-pointer mapping, and compact u32 export, allocation-returning and caller-owned `sampleIndices`/`sampleIndicesU32`, fixed-size `sampleArray` / `sampleArrayU32` index samples, fixed-size value/const-pointer/mutable-pointer arrays with `choose*Array` and `sample*Array` naming, allocation-returning/fixed-size/caller-owned value/const-pointer/mutable-pointer subset sampling, head-selected and Rust-style tail-selected selected/rest partial shuffles, fixed-size iterator arrays, allocation-returning/fixed-size/caller-owned weighted usize/u32/index-accessor/compact-index/item/pointer sampling, allocation-returning/fixed-size/caller-owned weighted iterator sampling, allocated/caller-owned value and pointer reservoir sampling, allocation-returning and caller-owned iterator sampling, checked exact-count iterator sampling | `src/seq.zig` tests |
| Collection sampling | one-shot usize/u32 index choice, value/const-pointer/mutable-pointer choice plus caller-owned and allocation-returning repeated choice batches through `Rng` and `seq` entry points, reusable choice value/pointer/index samples, fills, and owned value/pointer/index batches, stable and hinted choose iterators, `Rng` and `seq` shuffle entry points, partial shuffle, reservoir sampling, checked collection/iterator helpers | `src/rng.zig` and `src/seq.zig` tests |
| Weighted sampling | f64 usize/u32 and generic usize/u32 weighted index, index-weighted no-replacement samples, one-shot value/const-pointer/mutable-pointer choice, updateable alias table, updateable weighted choice with value/pointer/index samples, fills, and owned value/pointer/index batches, direct-source static and dynamic weighted sampling, checked weighted iterator and weighted no-replacement u32-index/value/pointer sampling | `src/distributions.zig`, `src/seq.zig` tests |
| Statistical smoke tests | engine bit balance, range buckets, normal/exponential means | `src/quality.zig` |
| Native benchmark evidence | Zig and Rust native CPU commands; facade/direct split | `compare/results/2026-06-27-rand-comparison.md` |

## Stage 1 Required Milestones

| ID | Milestone | Completion gate | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| M1 | External statistical validation | PractRand 0.96 `stdin64` at 16GiB or larger for `fast`, `default`, `wyhash64`, `pcg64`, `xoshiro256++`, and `chacha12`, with checked-in reports. Any anomaly must be investigated or explicitly accepted with rationale. | Closed: all listed engines have 16GiB passes |
| M2 | Distribution algorithm maturity | Replace correctness-first slow paths where mature algorithms are known: ziggurat-style normal/exponential or documented faster alternatives, and benchmarked exact large-n binomial. Keep exact semantics separate from approximation helpers. | Closed: single-shot normal/exponential use Zig stdlib ziggurat, reusable normal caches pairs, exponential precomputes inverse rate, and binomial has exact small-n/p=0.5/large-n rejection paths |
| M3 | Distribution benchmark matrix | Add benchmark rows for every public distribution family across at least one representative parameter set, including tail/derived/multivariate distributions. | Closed: `zig build bench` covers scalar, Bernoulli/binomial, Poisson, continuous, tail, derived, and multivariate distribution families |
| M4 | Fallible API surface | Provide checked/error-returning variants for public single-shot APIs where invalid input is realistically user-supplied, while preserving assert-based fast paths. | Closed and expanded: checked probability/range, weighted-index, sample-without-replacement, sequence-index, collection, iterator, weighted iterator/no-replacement, structured-value/enum, and charset constructors/helpers exist |
| M5 | Reproducibility matrix | Document deterministic output stability expectations for each reproducible engine and seed/stream derivation API, including what may vary by architecture or version. | Closed: `compare/results/reproducibility-matrix.md` defines stable, versioned-stable, and non-stable outputs |
| M6 | Core docs | Expand README or dedicated docs to cover engines, seeding, distributions, sequence sampling, statistical validation, and benchmark interpretation without relying only on tests and examples. | Closed: `docs/core-guide.md` covers core APIs, validation, and benchmarks |

## Stage 2 Required Milestones

| ID | Milestone | Completion gate | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S2-M1 | Extended statistical validation | PractRand 0.96 `stdin64` at 64GiB or larger for `fast`, `default`, `wyhash64`, `pcg64`, `xoshiro256++`, and `chacha12`, plus at least one TestU01-compatible report or a documented local blocker. | Closed: all listed engines have 64GiB PractRand passes |
| S2-M2 | Distribution parity-plus matrix | Compare the public distribution list against locally available `rand_distr`/historical `rand` distribution families and add any still-missing core families or explicitly document why they are out of scope for Zig-native `alea`. | Closed: `compare/results/distribution-parity-matrix.md` covers local `rand`, historical `rand`, Alea extras, and explicit out-of-scope items |
| S2-M3 | Parameter-grid distribution validation | For each public distribution family, add deterministic mean/variance or support checks across multiple parameter regimes, not just one representative case. | Closed: `zig build distcheck` covers scalar, discrete, continuous, bounded-support, vector distribution families, and constructor-ergonomics mean gates across multiple parameter regimes |
| S2-M4 | Benchmark parity matrix | Add Rust-side benchmark rows for comparable distribution and sequence workloads where `rand`/`rand_distr` exposes matching functionality, and keep Zig/Rust native CPU flags aligned. | Closed: Rust rows cover default-`rand` bytes/range/float/open-float/sequence/bool/string/weighted-index plus `rand_distr` normal, exponential, poisson, binomial, gamma, and beta |
| S2-M5 | Cross-platform reproducibility | Validate and document stable outputs on at least two architectures or OS targets, or document why the current environment cannot provide this evidence. | Closed for local environment: x86_64 Linux snapshot exists and second architecture/OS blocker is documented in `compare/results/cross-platform-repro-blocker.md` |
| S2-M6 | API reference completeness | Add public API reference docs or generated documentation covering all exported modules and examples. | Closed: `docs/api-reference.md` lists the public API surface and tooling, and `zig build apicheck` now gates public symbol coverage for exported modules and engines |

## Stage 3 Required Milestones

Stage 3 raises the Linux-first bar from broad parity-plus coverage to a stricter
local `rand_distr` 0.6.0 audit. The target is no known core RNG functionality
gap on the current Linux platform against the locally available `rand`,
`rand_distr`, and checked-in comparison evidence.

| ID | Milestone | Completion gate | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S3-M1 | Local `rand_distr` gap closure | Audit local `rand_distr` 0.6.0 source and implement or explicitly exclude each remaining core distribution/geometric sampler in Zig-native form. | Closed for known local distribution gaps: Gumbel, Frechet, SkewNormal, PERT, UnitCircle, UnitDisc, UnitSphere, UnitBall, inverse Gaussian, normal inverse Gaussian, Zipf, and Zeta are implemented |
| S3-M2 | Stage 3 validation grid | Extend `distcheck` and unit tests for all Stage 3 distributions with support checks, deterministic parameter grids, and mean/CDF-style smoke gates where moments exist. | Closed for Stage 3 distribution additions: unit tests and `distcheck` cover support and mean checks for the added families |
| S3-M3 | Stage 3 benchmark parity | Add Zig benchmark rows and Rust `rand_distr` rows for comparable Stage 3 workloads, using native CPU flags on both sides. | Closed for Stage 3 distribution additions: Zig and Rust rows cover comparable scalar and unit-geometry workloads |
| S3-M4 | Weighted dynamic sampling parity | Compare `AliasTable.update`, sequence weighted sampling, and local `rand_distr` weighted alias/tree APIs; add a Zig-native dynamic weighted sampler if alias rebuilds leave a real core gap. | Closed: `WeightedTree(Weight)` adds generic O(log n) sample/update/push/pop parity and `WeightedIntTree(Weight)` adds a faster unsigned-integer path comparable to local `rand_distr::weighted::WeightedTreeIndex`; Zig/Rust update+sample benchmark rows exist |
| S3-M5 | Linux no-known-gaps audit report | Replace informal coverage claims with a checked-in audit listing local Rust evidence, Alea status, remaining gaps, exclusions, and next Linux-first actions. | Closed: `compare/results/linux-no-known-gaps-audit.md` records the local Linux evidence, scope, exclusions, and current no-known-gaps finding |
| S3-M6 | Documentation and API reference refresh | Keep README, core guide, API reference, and parity matrix synchronized with every newly exported Stage 3 API. | Closed for Stage 3: README, core guide, API reference, parity matrix, Zig benchmark rows, and Rust benchmark rows are synchronized |

## Stage 4 Required Milestones

Stage 4 raises the bar after the local Linux no-known-gaps audit. The next focus
is broader evidence, longer validation, and Zig-native advantages beyond local
Rust parity.

| ID | Milestone | Completion gate | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S4-M1 | Broader platform reproducibility | Validate reproducibility snapshots and core distribution checks on at least one additional OS or architecture, or add a stronger blocker with exact missing infrastructure. | Closed for the current second-target bar: `compare/results/2026-07-03-repro-wasm32-wasi-node.md` records executed `wasm32-wasi` unit, repro, statcheck, and distcheck evidence via Node WASI; `compare/results/cross-platform-repro-blocker.md` now tracks remaining non-WASI runner gaps, and `zig build crosscheck` keeps compile-only smoke coverage for `wasm32-wasi`, `aarch64-linux`, `riscv64-linux`, `x86_64-windows`, `x86_64-macos`, and `aarch64-macos` |
| S4-M2 | Longer external statistical validation | Run and check in longer PractRand/TestU01-compatible evidence beyond the current local 64GiB engine reports for the primary Linux engines. | Closed for 128GiB Linux stage: all primary engines have 128GiB PractRand reports; `default` / `Xoshiro256` and `pcg64` each have one default-seed `unusual` plus a clean alternate-seed rerun, summarized in `compare/results/2026-06-28-practrand-128gib-summary.md`; after `Xoshiro256PlusPlus.fill` was made pointer-alignment independent, `compare/results/2026-07-03-practrand-xoshiro256plusplus-portable-fill-1gib.md` adds a clean 1GiB smoke for the new portable byte-fill mapping |
| S4-M3 | SIMD/vector sampling design | Design and prototype Zig-native vector/SIMD sampling APIs for high-volume scalar distributions without copying Rust `std::simd` surface shapes. | Closed for the current API/prototype bar: `Rng` and distribution namespaces now expose Zig-native vector APIs, direct/static vector helpers, bulk vector fills, vector checked variants, reusable vector samplers, and `vectorbench` coverage for uniform/strict-interval, probability, discrete, core continuous, tail/bounded, inverse/Zipf-Zeta, approximation, and unit-geometry workflows. A source audit now leaves only intentionally non-vector collection/multivariate helpers such as alias/weighted trees, Multinomial, and Dirichlet outside the vector-sampler shape. Dense true-SIMD normal/exponential distribution kernels remain a performance watch under S4-M4 rather than an API/prototype blocker; rejected repair/prefetch attempts and requirements for a future dense candidate are recorded in `simd-distribution-kernel-notes.md` and `performance-triage.md`. |
| S4-M4 | Performance follow-up from parity benchmarks | Use the completed feature matrix to choose targeted performance work where Alea trails local Rust in comparable core workloads. | Closed for current local Linux performance-follow-up bar: explicit opt-in coverage now addresses the known vector normal/exponential throughput gap, while default/general dense kernels move to S4-M5; LogNormal exact defaults are retained as a stable-output tradeoff with explicit opt-in performance profiles; exact `(0, 1]` `fillOpenClosed(f64)` endpoint-grid throughput now exceeds local Rust evidence after the `@mulAdd` raw-word conversion, while remaining precision-sensitive; other focused parity items below are closed or narrowed by evidence. | S4-M5 | Default/general dense SIMD distribution kernels | Raise the bar beyond opt-in throughput profiles: provide default or explicitly versioned dense SIMD normal/exponential kernels, or a documented policy accepting a named approximation profile for a specific default/general API surface, with statistical and reproducibility evidence. | Closed for the current local Linux policy bar: `s4-m5-approximation-policy.md` accepts named table and approx-log vector profiles as the explicit throughput-first dense vector normal/exponential surface for callers who choose approximation/output-mapping contracts; exact/default vector APIs intentionally remain scalar ziggurat lane-fill until an exact/default-compatible dense kernel wins. |
| S4-M6 | Accepted vector profile hardening | Harden the S4-M5 policy beyond the local Linux smoke bar: run accepted table/approx-log vector profiles on broader targets and/or longer distribution-quality checks, keep reproducibility snapshots current, and continue watching for exact/default-compatible dense SIMD kernels or new local Rust SIMD non-uniform rows. | Closed for the current bar: `tools/profilecheck.zig` now samples each accepted vector profile for 1,048,576 lanes with mean/variance and fixed-CDF gates, `zig build validate` includes `profilecheck`, `wasi-profilecheck` executes the same gates through Node WASI, `crosscheck` passes after the `std.DynLib` unsupported-target guard fix, and `compare/results/2026-07-04-s4-m6-profilecheck.md` records the native/WASI evidence. |
| S4-M7 | Longer tail/profile validation | Extend accepted vector-profile validation beyond deterministic 1Mi-lane smoke checks: add longer/adversarial tail-focused evidence, execute on another non-WASI runtime target when available, or replace the watch with an exact/default-compatible dense SIMD kernel that wins in the real harness. | Closed for the current bar: `tools/profiletailcheck.zig` samples each accepted vector profile for 8,388,608 lanes, checks normal two-sided tails and exponential upper tails, executes natively and through Node WASI, and `compare/results/2026-07-04-s4-m7-profiletailcheck.md` records the evidence. |
| S4-M8 | Multi-seed/profile stress or broader executed target | Extend accepted profile validation beyond fixed-seed smoke/tail gates by adding multi-seed stress evidence, executing on another non-WASI target, or landing an exact/default-compatible dense SIMD kernel that wins in the real harness. | Closed for the current bar: `tools/profilestresscheck.zig` samples each accepted vector profile across 8 deterministic seeds, checks per-seed moments plus aggregate CDF/tail gates, executes natively and through Node WASI, and `compare/results/2026-07-04-s4-m8-profilestresscheck.md` records the evidence. |
| S4-M9 | Broader runtime or exact dense-kernel breakthrough | Move beyond local Linux + WASI deterministic profile stress by executing accepted profile validation on another runtime/architecture target when infrastructure exists, running materially longer multi-seed/tail sweeps, or landing an exact/default-compatible dense SIMD kernel that wins in the real harness. | Closed for the current long-sweep bar: `tools/profilelongcheck.zig` samples each accepted vector profile across 8 seeds and 8,388,608 lanes/profile, checks per-seed moments plus aggregate tail gates, executes natively and through Node WASI, and `compare/results/2026-07-04-s4-m9-profilelongcheck.md` records the evidence; no additional non-WASI runtime target is available yet. |
| S4-M10 | Additional executed non-WASI target or exact dense-kernel win | Run accepted profile validation on another executed non-WASI runtime/architecture target, or land an exact/default-compatible dense SIMD normal/exponential kernel that beats scalar lane-fill in the real harness. | Closed for the current bar: `zig build -Dtarget=x86_64-linux-musl -Doptimize=ReleaseFast profilecheck-long` executes the accepted-profile long sweep on a second Linux ABI/runtime, and `compare/results/2026-07-04-s4-m10-profilelong-musl.md` records the matching evidence. |
| S4-M11 | Exact/default dense-kernel breakthrough or new external gap | Continue beyond accepted approximation-profile validation: land an exact/default-compatible dense SIMD normal/exponential kernel that wins in the real harness, execute profile validation on a genuinely different architecture/runtime when available, or find and close a new local `rand`/`rand_distr` core gap. | Blocked in this session: `compare/results/s4-m11-blocker-audit.md` records that no exact/default-compatible dense SIMD winner is known, no additional runtime runner such as qemu/wine/wasmtime/wasmer is installed beyond native glibc, musl, and Node WASI, and local `rand`/`rand_distr` still lack SIMD non-uniform normal/exponential rows. |

| S4-M535 | Next unblocked product gap after S4-M11 blocker | Continue product improvements that do not depend on unavailable exact dense-kernel insight or extra runtime runners: audit docs/examples/tooling/roadmap for other advanced APIs, improve adoption/testing ergonomics, or wait for a new local Rust/core RNG gap or runtime to become available. | In progress: S4-M11 remains blocked, and the next independent product improvement has not yet been selected. |
## Current Rule

Continue feature-first or performance work on the earliest unblocked stage milestone. When an earlier milestone is locally blocked, keep its blocker evidence current and proceed to the next unblocked milestone. Use
`zig build validate` for broad native validation, `zig build validate-local`
when a change affects the local `rand` / `rand_distr` comparison workflow or
public-surface evidence, and at minimum
`zig build statcheck` after changes that affect engines, distributions, ranges,
or sampling internals. Use `zig build stream -- ...` to feed raw engine output
into external statistical tools when validating engine changes. Defer pure
micro-optimization until feature, correctness, and validation milestones are in
place, except where performance is part of a feature's viability.

## Long-Term Product Tracks

These tracks exist beyond any single roadmap stage. Closing a stage means the
current evidence bar was met, not that Alea has finished surpassing Rust
`rand` / `rand_distr` as a product.

| Track | Product target | Current next pressure |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Feature breadth | Core random workflows should be available in one Zig-native library without forcing users into companion packages. | Bulk range, strict-interval float, standard normal/exponential, normal, log-normal, half-normal, inverse-Gaussian-family, skew-normal, unit geometry, discrete distribution, and reusable-sampler fill APIs exist; Laplace, Logistic, Rayleigh, HalfNormal, Maxwell, Chi, Erlang, LogLogistic, Kumaraswamy, Arcsine, and PowerFunction extend continuous distribution breadth beyond the local Rust list; continue adding specialized bulk paths only where they materially improve throughput or ergonomics. |
| Statistical confidence | Engine and distribution evidence should keep getting longer, broader, and easier to reproduce. | Follow `compare/results/practrand-observation-followup.md` for `default` and `pcg64`; keep stable-output unit snapshots and stream-shape regressions in `compare/results/reproducibility-matrix.md` current; add second-platform execution when infrastructure exists. |
| Performance | Fast paths should be competitive with or faster than local Rust evidence for comparable workloads, with facade/direct overhead separated. | Follow `compare/results/performance-triage.md`; distinguish bulk-fast, scalar-fast, and allocation-free direct-source profiles when choosing defaults or recommendations. |
| Ergonomics | APIs should feel natural in Zig, including allocation-free and comptime-friendly workflows. | `fillSample` and iterator `fill` methods give reusable samplers and value iterators allocation-free bulk paths where their stream policies allow it, while checked collection, iterator, weighted no-replacement, discrete, core continuous, tail/bounded, inverse-Gaussian-family, Zipf/Zeta, and multivariate output-buffer helpers reduce boilerplate for fallible high-volume workflows; continue reducing boilerplate where it materially improves ergonomics. |
| Portability | Stable-output expectations should be clear across targets, and blockers should be exact. | Keep the Linux and wasm32-wasi stable-output suites green with `zig build validate-all` (or its component steps `zig build validate`, `zig build crosscheck`, `zig build test-wasi`, and `zig build wasi-report`); then raise the next portability bar to QEMU/Wine/native second-OS runners beyond the current Node WASI evidence. |
